Gamers just don't get it. It's an intentional reference, multiple layers - too complex for the average person. I'll try to explain. So the game's called overWATCH right. See what I did there? WATCH. So what you do is you watch the queue, and while you're WATCHing the queue, you actually sit there and think about TIME. Get it? Watches? Time? So then also while you're thinking about TIME, TIME passes, so you're experiencing time on multiple levels. WATCHING TIME pass, feeling TIME pass, maybe looking at a CLOCK on your computer (which is just a new age WATCH). You know, I think it's just too difficult to explain. This has to be quite literally the most beautiful pieces of art I ever seen In many ways, the work of a critic is easy. We risk very little, yet enjoy a position over those who offer up their work and their selves to our judgment. We thrive on negative criticism, which is fun to write and to read. But the bitter truth we critics must face, is that in the grand scheme of things, the average piece of junk is probably more meaningful than our criticism designating it so. But there are times when a critic truly risks something, and that is in the discovery and defense of the *new*. The world is often unkind to new talent, new creations. The new needs friends. Last night, I experienced something new: an extraordinary video from a singularly unexpected source. To say that both the video and its maker have challenged my preconceptions about fine Video Editing is a gross understatement. They have rocked me to my core. In the past, I have made no secret of my disdain for this channel and it‚Äôs famous motto, "Anyone can make a YouTube Video" But I realize, only now do I truly understand what they meant. Not everyone can become a great artist; but a great artist *can* come from *anywhere*. It is difficult to imagine more humble origins than those of the genius now making videos on this channel, who is, in this critic's opinion, nothing less than the finest YouTuber in France. I will be returning to this channel soon, hungry for more.

You guys loves Warhammer 40,000 right? Now introducing Overwatch 2 40,000
From the earliest trailer to its release, the first Overwatch only ever reminded me of the horrible, legitimately traumatic time years before when I mixed cocaine on top of some mushrooms. When I did that I experienced a world way to vivid and hyper all at once, basically exactly like this game, turning me into a kind of fountainhead of color, light, and cartoon sounds where instead of being nice every new shade of each of the thousands of colors rushing before my eyes I experienced as a different expression of pain. Imagine Hellraiser meeting The Care Bears. That was the day I learned there are as many pains in the universe as there are colors, that our suffering is as inseparable from reality as are photons, and why the light exists only as a mirror to our torments. Overwatch makes me feel the same -- and I mean even thinking about it, and about the people who play or promote it, not to mention playing it for myself. It's why I have only ever longed for the grey and brown days of early 2000s gaming. Those were nicer, calmer days.  It felt like a heart-attack in my brain. How these games look so uncannily similar in style to that experience, and just the feel and tone of it are so similar, makes me think either the devs are people who mix cocaine and mushrooms and like it or that they would like it if they did -- and that has me convinced they are either insane or corrupted by devils. I think it's insidious and that anyone who plays this will destroy the world. With most games I don't enjoy, but which others do, I usually believe, "Good for them, because that's still a plus for gaming as a whole," but with Overwatch and all its clones I think failure is the only option for humanity as well as being a good lesson on not to even simulate, let alone try, ever mixing cocaine and mushrooms and/or being the kind of person who can dwell in that level of mania and thrive. They're all just, "wrong," or, "off," like these sort of disguised, unholy abominations, these, "things that should not be," cosmically incorrect instances of un-life that still somehow came to live among us only pretending to belong. A curse upon them. A curse upon their houses, and upon all their generations wherever they go.  One minute you're laughing like rainbows are being farted out of your eyeballs, the next minute everyone is dead, and then they've won, and none of us should have to tolerate it. As for people who do, at least to those who come away thinking it was enjoyable and not hellish, and who'd want to spread more of those obscene, inane, incessant colors and noises to everyone else like a brain-virus where the rest of us will never again get a moment's peace: extermination is the only answer. Exterminate them and destroy all they've made before they can exterminate us. That's got to be the line in the sand, though some might say products like Overwatch have already crossed that line; and, yes, it probably means there really is a conspiracy among the technocratic elite to diminish the rest of our minds and keep us more like domesticated pets. Think about it (if you even still can think after this ego-death-inducing guff has rattled your minds). Hate. Hate! Hate!!! This will be the only thing that can save us.  That's why we should all salute those brave, anonymous souls who try to take junk like this down with things like ddos attacks, and if we ever find out who those people are, maybe someday, I'm thinking statues in their honor. It's the least they deserve. If you don't agree, you don't know anything. You have already been infected. All you can do now is pray for redemption -- that, or at least keep what you mix with your mushrooms to only weed, or maybe a little ecstasy, or heroine, if not for you then for the rest of humanity and all our futures. Game responsibly. Everyone dies, but the people who made and marketed Overwatch should die sooner, preferably by divine accident, which would have already happened were this a fairer world.  9 out of 10 for that one girl character having a sexy haircut and a butt, though. And perky tits. Also, vagina somewhere.  And that's my essay about the game Overwatch. I'm up for hire. To any sites or companies: I'm up for hire.

I'm also noticing a lot of visual bugs with highlight intros, skins, animations, and player models (I even noticed that on the Ilios loading screen there are now 7 blank A - Posing player-models scattered around the map). Another bug is that sometimes you can't invite other players to your party, a problem that annoyed me greatly, I've found a temporary workaround by using "/invite" in chat  Also made the discovery, on the free battle pass, it took be around 30 games of competitive (and a couple of quickplays and 3v3 here and there) to get to level 10 on the Free Pass. New Characters like Kiriko require you to reach level 55 of the pass in order to play them. I'm estimating 165 matches before I reach level 55 on the free pass, thankfully I had Overwatch 1 before so its I have her unlocked anyway, but that won't be true for future characters where I will have to unlock them in the Battle Pass.  So, when the next broken character is rolled out, if I have to grind for weeks just to play as them, I'm going to be even more disappointed.  Speaking of broken - thank the lord Kiriko isn't in comp because she is very busted. Got her to low health and needed to reload my guns. By the time I reloaded she had nearly all her health back. It takes 1 second to reload tracer's guns. It does not take a genius to realise that just giving a blanket heal over time to every healer without taking into consideration each character's different abilities is a horrible idea when it comes to balancing.
